### [222] [cuRoboV2: Dynamics-Aware Motion Generation with Depth-Fused Distance Fields for High-DoF Robots](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.05493)
*Balakumar Sundaralingam,Adithyavairavan Murali,Stan Birchfield*

Main category: cs.RO

TL;DR: cuRoboV2 is a unified GPU-native robotics framework that combines trajectory optimization, dense perception, and whole-body computation to generate safe, feasible motions for manipulators and humanoids.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Current robotics methods are fragmented: fast planners produce unexecutable trajectories, reactive controllers struggle with perception, and existing solvers fail on high-DoF systems, creating a need for a unified, scalable solution.

Method: Three key innovations: (1) B-spline trajectory optimization with smoothness and torque limits, (2) GPU-native TSDF/ESDF perception pipeline generating dense signed distance fields, (3) scalable GPU-native whole-body computation including topology-aware kinematics, differentiable inverse dynamics, and map-reduce self-collision.

Result: Achieves 99.7% success under 3kg payload (vs 72-77% baselines), 99.6% collision-free IK on 48-DoF humanoid (prior methods fail), 89.5% retargeting constraint satisfaction (vs 61% PyRoki), and enables LLM coding assistants to author 73% of new modules.

Conclusion: cuRoboV2 provides a unified, dynamics-aware motion generation stack that scales from single-arm manipulators to full humanoids, demonstrating that well-structured robotics code enables productive human-LLM collaboration.

Abstract: Effective robot autonomy requires motion generation that is safe, feasible, and reactive. Current methods are fragmented: fast planners output physically unexecutable trajectories, reactive controllers struggle with high-fidelity perception, and existing solvers fail on high-DoF systems. We present cuRoboV2, a unified framework with three key innovations: (1) B-spline trajectory optimization that enforces smoothness and torque limits; (2) a GPU-native TSDF/ESDF perception pipeline that generates dense signed distance fields covering the full workspace, unlike existing methods that only provide distances within sparsely allocated blocks, up to 10x faster and in 8x less memory than the state-of-the-art at manipulation scale, with up to 99% collision recall; and (3) scalable GPU-native whole-body computation, namely topology-aware kinematics, differentiable inverse dynamics, and map-reduce self-collision, that achieves up to 61x speedup while also extending to high-DoF humanoids (where previous GPU implementations fail). On benchmarks, cuRoboV2 achieves 99.7% success under 3kg payload (where baselines achieve only 72--77%), 99.6% collision-free IK on a 48-DoF humanoid (where prior methods fail entirely), and 89.5% retargeting constraint satisfaction (vs. 61% for PyRoki); these collision-free motions yield locomotion policies with 21% lower tracking error than PyRoki and 12x lower cross-seed variance than mink. A ground-up codebase redesign for discoverability enabled LLM coding assistants to author up to 73% of new modules, including hand-optimized CUDA kernels, demonstrating that well-structured robotics code can unlock productive human--LLM collaboration. Together, these advances provide a unified, dynamics-aware motion generation stack that scales from single-arm manipulators to full humanoids.

### [223] [Safe-SAGE: Social-Semantic Adaptive Guidance for Safe Engagement through Laplace-Modulated Poisson Safety Functions](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.05497)
*Lizhi Yang,Ryan M. Bena,Meg Wilkinson,Gilbert Bahati,Andy Navarro Brenes,Ryan K. Cosner,Aaron D. Ames*

Main category: cs.RO

TL;DR: Safe-SAGE framework integrates semantic understanding with safety-critical control for legged robots, using Poisson safety functions and Laplace guidance fields to enable context-dependent obstacle treatment with varying safety margins.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Traditional safety-critical control methods like control barrier functions suffer from semantic blindness - they treat all obstacles uniformly regardless of contextual significance, leading to suboptimal behavior in semantically rich environments.

Method: Multi-sensor fusion of point clouds with vision-based instance segmentation and persistent object tracking, combined with a multi-layer safety filter (MPC + CBF) using Poisson safety functions and Laplace guidance field modulation for context-dependent obstacle treatment.

Result: Enables legged robots to navigate semantically rich, dynamic environments with context-dependent safety margins while maintaining rigorous safety guarantees, overcoming semantic blindness of traditional methods.

Conclusion: Safe-SAGE successfully bridges high-level semantic understanding with low-level safety-critical control, allowing robots to treat obstacles differently based on semantic meaning while ensuring safety in complex environments.

Abstract: Traditional safety-critical control methods, such as control barrier functions, suffer from semantic blindness, exhibiting the same behavior around obstacles regardless of contextual significance. This limitation leads to the uniform treatment of all obstacles, despite their differing semantic meanings. We present Safe-SAGE (Social-Semantic Adaptive Guidance for Safe Engagement), a unified framework that bridges the gap between high-level semantic understanding and low-level safety-critical control through a Poisson safety function (PSF) modulated using a Laplace guidance field. Our approach perceives the environment by fusing multi-sensor point clouds with vision-based instance segmentation and persistent object tracking to maintain up-to-date semantics beyond the camera's field of view. A multi-layer safety filter is then used to modulate system inputs to achieve safe navigation using this semantic understanding of the environment. This safety filter consists of both a model predictive control layer and a control barrier function layer. Both layers utilize the PSF and flux modulation of the guidance field to introduce varying levels of conservatism and multi-agent passing norms for different obstacles in the environment. Our framework enables legged robots to navigate semantically rich, dynamic environments with context-dependent safety margins while maintaining rigorous safety guarantees.

### [224] [RoboPocket: Improve Robot Policies Instantly with Your Phone](https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.05504)
*Junjie Fang,Wendi Chen,Han Xue,Fangyuan Zhou,Tian Le,Yi Wang,Yuting Zhang,Jun Lv,Chuan Wen,Cewu Lu*

Main category: cs.RO

TL;DR: RoboPocket enables robot-free instant policy iteration using smartphones with AR visual foresight to identify policy weaknesses and focus data collection efficiently.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Current imitation learning faces a trade-off: handheld interfaces scale data collection but operate open-loop without targeting policy weaknesses, while interactive methods like DAgger address covariate shift but require physical robots which are costly and hard to scale.

Method: RoboPocket uses smartphones with a Remote Inference framework that visualizes policy-predicted trajectories via AR Visual Foresight, allowing collectors to identify failures and focus on weak regions. It also implements asynchronous Online Finetuning that continuously updates policies with incoming data.

Result: The system doubles data efficiency compared to offline scaling strategies and boosts sample efficiency by up to 2× in distributed environments with minimal interactive corrections per person.

Conclusion: RoboPocket reconciles the scalability of handheld interfaces with the effectiveness of interactive methods by enabling robot-free instant policy iteration, overcoming long-standing efficiency bottlenecks in imitation learning data collection.

Abstract: Scaling imitation learning is fundamentally constrained by the efficiency of data collection. While handheld interfaces have emerged as a scalable solution for in-the-wild data acquisition, they predominantly operate in an open-loop manner: operators blindly collect demonstrations without knowing the underlying policy's weaknesses, leading to inefficient coverage of critical state distributions. Conversely, interactive methods like DAgger effectively address covariate shift but rely on physical robot execution, which is costly and difficult to scale. To reconcile this trade-off, we introduce RoboPocket, a portable system that enables Robot-Free Instant Policy Iteration using single consumer smartphones. Its core innovation is a Remote Inference framework that visualizes the policy's predicted trajectory via Augmented Reality (AR) Visual Foresight. This immersive feedback allows collectors to proactively identify potential failures and focus data collection on the policy's weak regions without requiring a physical robot. Furthermore, we implement an asynchronous Online Finetuning pipeline that continuously updates the policy with incoming data, effectively closing the learning loop in minutes. Extensive experiments demonstrate that RoboPocket adheres to data scaling laws and doubles the data efficiency compared to offline scaling strategies, overcoming their long-standing efficiency bottleneck. Moreover, our instant iteration loop also boosts sample efficiency by up to 2$\times$ in distributed environments a small number of interactive corrections per person. Project page and videos: https://robo-pocket.github.io.
